Newspaper Workers' General Strike Today 126

Opposing the "Shishi Xinbao" Newspaper's Dismissal of a Large Number of Workers

Supporting Workers Forced to Leave the "Shishi Xinbao" Newspaper

The labor dispute at the "Shishi Xinbao" newspaper, which has long attracted social attention, has lasted for two months since it occurred on April 2nd. Various community groups have repeatedly mediated, but due to the newspaper's firm stance,

Without any concession, it has led to this strike. Now the "Shen Bao," "Xinwen Bao," and "Shishi Xinbao" newspapers in Shanghai have unanimously joined in, and the situation is quite serious. The details are listed as follows:

Cause of the Labor Dispute: On April 2nd of this year, the "Shishi Xinbao" newspaper's management forced the newspaper's workers to concurrently print the "Da Wan Bao" newspaper. (Note: The "Da Wan Bao" newspaper is sponsored by Zhang Zhuping, chairman of the "Shishi Xinbao" board of directors, and has its own printing equipment. It has been published for two months. There is no need for the "Shishi Xinbao" newspaper to print it on its behalf. It is actually a tool for provocation. Because the newspaper's management knew that the labor union would not agree, it used this as a pretext to lock down the factory and force the newspaper's workers to leave, in order to achieve its goal of undermining the labor movement.) At that time, the newspaper's workers politely refused because the labor union had regulations that one newspaper should not print two newspapers. They immediately reported to the labor union for instructions. The labor union immediately sent a committee member, Zhang Baokang, to explain everything to the newspaper's management. Unexpectedly, a newspaper employee (actually not an employee, but the newspaper's registered lawyer) came forward to argue. First, there was a verbal conflict, then Committee Member Zhang was beaten and insulted, and his clothes were torn. At the same time, a large number of police officers were instigated to arrest Committee Member Zhang. At that time, under the strong protection of a large number of workers, he was able to escape. Therefore, the newspaper's workers went to the labor union to report the incident. The "Shishi Xinbao" newspaper's management took the opportunity to lock down the factory while a group of workers were leaving the factory, refusing to allow them to work, and announced that all the newspaper's workers would be dismissed.

Negotiation Process: After learning that the "Shishi Xinbao" newspaper dismissed all its workers, the newspaper labor union immediately sent representatives to the newspaper's management to make a serious representation. Because the newspaper was determined to undermine the labor union, it initially demanded that the labor union dismiss Committee Member Zhang Baokang and order all workers to fill out a statement of willingness before allowing them to work. The labor union believed that since the labor union had previously signed a labor-management agreement with the newspaper, and both sides had been able to abide by it, the newspaper's dismissal of all workers for no reason violated the labor-management agreement and was an attempt to undermine the labor union. There was no result and the meeting broke up. After this, the postal service, distribution, and private individuals came forward to mediate with the management, but there was no result. It has been two months since this incident occurred, leading to the general strike of the "Shen Bao," "Xinwen Bao," and "Shishi Xinbao" newspapers to support the workers.

Strike Declaration: All oppressed workers and compatriots in China, in recent years, the lives of us workers have been affected by many complex political and economic factors, and we have been suffering beyond description. Since the "September 18th" Manchurian Incident, Chinese capitalists have repeatedly retreated and not resisted the aggression and oppression of Japanese imperialism. However, they have adopted a proactive strategy towards us workers, who are cold and hungry. They, the capitalists, use "resisting Japan and saving the country" and "promoting domestic goods," "increasing production" as an excuse to intensify their exploitation. Only despicable capitalists will implement such shameless and cruel methods, and only we Chinese workers will deeply suffer from such a tragic fate.

After the "January 28th" Shanghai Incident, the entire Shanghai became a battlefield, and all production organs completely tended to

Suspension. The majority of our Shanghai workers were homeless and destitute. A large number of laborers suddenly increased in the vast labor market. Therefore, the clever capitalists took this opportunity to increase unemployment and lay off the original organized or higher-wage workers, and hired new unorganized and lower-wage workers to satisfy their insatiable greed. Therefore, we workers were both brutally killed by the Japanese imperialists and further exploited by the Chinese capitalists. Under this dual severe pressure, even the strength to groan and struggle disappeared.

This kind of fact was first implemented by the capitalists of the "Shishi Xinbao" newspaper, who assumed the responsibility of "leading society," and the workers who worked all day in the "cultural industry" were also the first to be poisoned by it. Before the outbreak of the "January 28th" Incident, the "Minguo Ribao" newspaper was sealed up by the imperialists because it published anti-Japanese news. However, the management of the "Minguo Ribao" newspaper repeatedly succumbed to the oppression of the imperialists and even admitted to its "temporary suspension," but did not care about the fact that the imperialists' cannons were still attacking us fiercely and ruthlessly laid off the workers of the "Minguo Ribao" newspaper, causing the workers of the "Minguo Ribao" newspaper to be displaced and destitute. In less than two months, the capitalists of the "Shishi Xinbao" newspaper also came up with a novel idea, using the issue of printing the "Da Wan Bao" newspaper as a pretext to openly undermine our labor union organization. Failing to undermine it, they implemented a mass layoff. Although some workers have been forced to go to work under the threat of bribery and coercion, there are still thirty or forty people who have refused to give in and refuse to go to work. The workers who have gone to work have silently surrendered under the power of the one or two workers bought by the management. The conspiracy of the "Shishi Xinbao" newspaper has been fully realized. But looking back at the lives of the dozens of workers who have not yet gone to work and looking forward to the future of our association, we feel extremely dangerous. Now, in order to protect our own vital interests and consolidate the foundation of the labor union, we have to make a final duel with the fierce and vicious capitalists of the "Shishi Xinbao" newspaper, and we have to lead all the newspaper workers to go on strike together to promote their awareness. We hope that all Chinese workers and compatriots will provide spiritual and material assistance at any time.

Strike Objectives: (1) All workers forced to leave the "Shishi Xinbao" newspaper must be reinstated. (2) The wages of the workers forced to leave the newspaper must be paid in full for the period they were out of work. (3) Compensation must be paid for all losses suffered by the labor union as a result of this incident. (4) The labor-management agreement previously signed between the labor union and the "Shishi Xinbao" newspaper remains valid.

Strike Order: For urgent notice, this association believes that the management of the "Shishi Xinbao" newspaper deliberately undermined the unity of this association and dismissed a large number of workers. Although this association has conducted peaceful negotiations for two months, it has not been able to obtain the understanding of the newspaper's management. It is now decided to declare a general strike of the "Shen Bao," "Xinwen Bao," and "Shishi Xinbao" newspapers from June 1st to promote the early resolution of the newspaper's management. All workers are required to abide by this order without fail. This is an urgent order.

Strike Discipline: (1) All members of this association must absolutely obey the orders of the strike committee after the strike. (2) Before receiving the strike committee's order to resume work, they must absolutely not resume work without authorization, otherwise they will be considered to have undermined the strike. (3) No acts of undermining the strike are allowed. (4) Do not spread rumors or incite people's minds. (5) Obey the command of the picket team. (6) Strictly maintain order. (7) Those who violate the discipline will be punished in the most severe way.

Public Announcement to All Circles: To all people from all walks of life, this association has been established for five years since its establishment in the 16th year of the Republic of China. The labor and management sides have signed an agreement, and both sides can abide by it and live in peace. However, on April 2nd of this year, the management of the "Shishi Xinbao" newspaper used the fact that it could not print the "Da Wan Bao" newspaper as an excuse, citing that this association interfered with the newspaper's administration, and dismissed all workers. This association and various community groups have repeatedly mediated and tried to get the workers to go back to work, but it has been ineffective. It has been two months since then. This association thinks that there is no hope for a peaceful solution, and the emotions of all members are excited and cannot be restrained. Therefore, we have no choice but to declare a general strike from today to promote the awareness of the newspaper and achieve the purpose of restoring the jobs of the workers who left the newspaper. This association has also considered that newspapers transmit domestic and foreign news and are indispensable for people from all walks of life, but for the sake of the interests of all newspaper workers in our association, it is impossible to have both, so we have no choice but to resort to this last resort. Therefore, this association is very sorry for the obstruction of the hearing of the social people. I hope that people from all walks of life will sympathize and help, so that this unfortunate [situation] can be resolved in the fastest possible time, then it will be fortunate.

Statement to Various Agencies: Report to the Municipal Government, Party Headquarters, and Social Affairs Bureau, stating, "Regarding the reporting of the matter, the Shishi Xinbao authorities, on April 2nd of this year, locked down the factory and dismissed a large number of workers on the pretext of the Da Wan Bao incident, hoping to undermine the organization of the subordinate association. This has been reported in the case repeatedly. However, for two months, various community groups have run around to mediate, but in the end, the attitude of the museum is tough and there is no sincerity, so it has not been resolved yet. All members of the subordinate association think that there is no hope for a peaceful solution, and the feelings of the public are excited and cannot be restrained. Now, because it is forced to, a general strike is announced from today to promote the awareness of the museum, and I sincerely ask the chiefs of the 'association and bureau' to uphold justice and pass on the matter to the workers who were forced to leave, so that they can resume work as soon as possible. I am waiting for your orders. June 1st, the eleventh year of the Republic of China. Educational news highlights

Explanation of Jiangsu Education Department's Prohibition of Teaching Strikes and Salary Demands 128

Preventing the Use of Salary Demands as a Pretext to Stir Up Educational Unrest

Since the Jiangsu Education Department issued a clear order prohibiting elementary school teachers and staff from going on strike to demand salaries, there has been much suspicion from the outside world regarding this instruction. In order to understand the truth, the reporter went to the Education Department to inquire about opinions from the responsible personnel. They provided separate explanations as follows:

The motivation for this department's prohibition of teaching strikes and salary demands is due to the fact that trouble makers in the education circles of various counties often use the name of demanding arrears to carry out acts of surrounding [authorities], causing educational unrest, which makes it impossible for educational administrative authorities to handle daily affairs, and even causes a state of unease in the education of the entire county. Therefore, it is necessary to strictly prohibit them, and it is not to force elementary school teachers to teach on an empty stomach, nor is it to cancel all arrears at all, as the outside world says, depriving them of their due rights or hindering their livelihoods. As for the issue of clearing the salary arrears of elementary school teachers, this department is planning to separately clean up the arrears. Regarding this level, it should be divided into old arrears and new arrears. The old arrears are probably caused by long-term overspending and erosion, and it is impossible to handle them clearly in a short period of time. We are currently tracking down and recovering the educational funds that have been misappropriated or misused over the years. Once we have a certain amount, we will gradually pay them back. On the one hand, we are trying our best to prevent new arrears from occurring. The first measure is to strictly prohibit overspending, so we have recently carefully reviewed the budgets of various counties and implemented a principle of balanced income and expenditure. If we can implement it, and if there are no unexpected events, there should be no more arrears of salaries. This department will never ignore the hardship of elementary school teachers' lives and the excessive arrears of salaries, and we are constantly thinking about ways to clear them. For example, in this reorganization of Jiangdu education, on the one hand, we are replacing derelict officials, but on the other hand, we are still using all methods to strictly pursue the old debts from those who refuse to write [acknowledgements]. We are also formulating methods for collecting and disbursing education funds in the future. However, it is difficult to reverse the accumulated problems, and it is not possible to fundamentally and completely reorganize them in a short period of time. If elementary school teachers are really forced by livelihood and make legitimate appeals, this department will certainly examine the actual situation and urge the administrative authorities of various counties to properly plan for relief. If the education authorities of various counties have acts of dereliction of duty or private gain, once this department detects them, we will definitely enforce the law to wrap them up. If the people of various counties have any opinions, they can provide evidence and submit a written report according to the complaint procedures. This department will also handle it according to law without any favoritism. In short, this department's move is to prevent the troublemaking of unscrupulous elements, and it is not initially to ignore the hardship of the livelihood of elementary school teachers and arbitrarily oppress them, nor is it to erase all the previous salary arrears. The words of the outside world, such as "only officials are allowed to set fires, but the people are not allowed to light lamps," are really misunderstandings. I sincerely hope that you will explain the intention of this department on our behalf, etc.

Passed Eight Detailed Rules for the Service of Social Education Personnel in Various Counties

Preparing to Convene a Conference of Education Bureau Chiefs from Across Jiangsu Province

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education held its sixth departmental affairs meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday (the 25th). Once these detailed rules are passed in the meeting, they will be circulated to various counties for strict compliance. Records of the Ancient Temple's Bell-ringing (11) – The Unswept Courtyard Study Gentleman 132

Thirteen

"Once the school opens, there will be nowhere to burn incense." This is Old Xu's hypnotic trick to fool women. How anxious I am! If the old ladies and young mistresses believe his words and join the group opposing us, we will be completely defeated. I was thinking with my eyes closed about countermeasures to resist.

Suddenly, I heard a voice shouting "Chairman!" I saw that plump old lady Song was about to speak. Grandma Wu, who was sitting in front of her, also shouted "Chairman!" Sister-in-law Wang Er pulled on Grandma Wu's clothes and gently said to her, "Zhong'er said that two people cannot speak at the same time. Wait for Old Lady Song to speak, and then you can speak." Grandma Wu sat down. What a patient and persuasive Sister-in-law Wang Er! Grandma Wu's willingness to take advice is also unmatched. Compare that to those adults and gentlemen who break each other's heads with inkstones, how different! Who says our rural civil rights will cause trouble? Old Lady Song usually likes to help the poor and enjoys great prestige in the village, and has significant influence. I was anxious to hear her opinion. She said: "Counseling them not to listen blindly to Zhong'er's nonsense, I am now coming out to respond as an old lady. We all have eyes, and our ears are not deaf either. How can you call it blindly listening? Although Zhong'er is young, he is also a person. Why are his words nonsense? Opening a school is not limited to destroying the Buddha. Why is there nowhere to burn incense? This old woman wants to worship Buddha, and her grandchildren want to go to school. Holding school in the Buddha hall, we can watch the children study while burning incense. It can be said that it is doubly convenient and couldn't be better. I oppose Brother Xu's suggestion."

The chairman called on Grandma Wu to speak. Grandma Wu said, "Everything I wanted to say has already been said by Old Lady Song. I support opening a school and not destroying the Buddha."

After the discussion was over, the chairman put it to a vote. Only Old Xu raised a hand to oppose the opening of the school. One hand! How lonely that was! The most interesting thing was the owner of the grocery store. Because not destroying the Buddha does no harm to his business of gold foil and incense paper, he didn't care about Old Xu's loneliness either.

The next item discussed was the qualifications of the teacher. Everyone agreed that they should hire the very best and most capable person to be the teacher. As for what is considered the very best and most capable, you only need to look at the records of that day to understand what kind of teacher our villagers ideally had in mind:

Zhang Huzi said, "The teacher must be proficient in the Four Books and Five Classics. Eight-legged essays are useless now. He must be able to write essays on current affairs." Yu Laowu, who had recently lost a lawsuit, said, "It's best to understand the law." Zhu Laotai, who was looking for a wife for her son everywhere, said, "He should be able to match horoscopes and write invitation cards. That would be convenient." Ding Laowu, who was planning to buy land, said, "He must be a teacher who can write deeds."

Old Lady Song, who was experienced and afraid that Zhang Huzi would interfere and also afraid of fashionable teachers from the city, said, "We want to hire a 'five-no' teacher: one who doesn't skip class, two who doesn't smoke, three who doesn't gamble, four who doesn't let 'drizzling rain' fall, and five who doesn't say 'my dear sister, I love you...'" She spoke freely and unrestrainedly, causing everyone to burst into laughter.

I think finding a graduate from a good normal school or above can meet all of these requirements. Finally, everyone passed the motion to find a normal school graduate who meets the above qualifications to be the teacher.

Remuneration was also discussed. Everyone would take turns providing meals. Each student would send gifts for the three main festivals, ranging from one to two yuan per festival, with the very poor being exempt from sending gifts. Temple funds would be used for equipment expenses.

Brother Chun Sheng, Old Lady Song, and I were elected as members of the preparatory committee, responsible for finding a teacher who is the very best and most capable.

The Ambition and Strength of Japanese Athletes at the 10th World Olympic Games (Part 1) Translated by Jiang Huaiqing 137

Track and Field Seeks Decisive Victory over the US, Germany, and Finland

Swimming Hopes to Overpower the United States and Seize the Championship

Should Our National Authorities Be Alerted?

This article is an English manuscript written by Mr. Kyo Kutsushi, a Japanese, originally titled "Japan's Athletic Forces Preparing to Invade US For Olympiad." The article is very long. The following is an abridged translation, offered to our national authorities and the sports community, to see if they can be alerted to self-motivate themselves. -Translator's Postscript

The 10th World Olympic Games will be held in Los Angeles, California, USA, from July 31st to August 14th. Japan is currently actively preparing for joint training. Approximately 140 people will attend the Games. It is also planned that after the closing ceremony, from August 15th, the Japanese team will invite athletes from other countries to hold a quadrangular track and field competition in San Francisco. Germany has decided to join, and the United States and Britain are also expected to participate. At the same time, Finnish athletes will also tour Japan and Europe at that time. After they arrive in Japan, they will also hold competitive matches. Therefore, Japanese athletes are very proud and have great hopes and interests.

A Brief History of Japan's Participation in the World Games: Japan's participation in the World Olympic Games dates back 20 years. However, at that time, new-era sports such as track and field were immature. Only fencing, wrestling, and boxing were included. In the past 20 years, new-era sports have been vigorously promoted and gradually expanded. Now they are surprisingly dominating the world stage. When the 6th World Games were held in Stockholm in 1912, only two people were sent to participate. This was the first time Japanese athletes appeared on the world stage. At the Swedish Games in 1920, the number of Japanese athletes attending increased to 15. At the French Games in 1924, the number of athletes suddenly doubled, reaching as many as 30. In these past Games, Japanese athletes have gradually shown their talent. Although they did not score many points, they attracted the attention of major sports powers. By the time of the Dutch Games in 1928, the number of Japanese athletes had exceeded 50. They also created great new world records, proudly boasting to people of all countries, which made people gasp. For example, Oda Mikio won the triple jump championship and set a new world record with a score of 15.58 meters.

The Content of the Team: Among the 140 Japanese athletes, many are world record holders. Therefore, their strength is sufficient, far surpassing that of the past. There are a total of 30 or 40 people in the team, including managers, coaches, and attendants. The Japanese Sports Association has invited Mr. Morita Toshihiko as the general team leader. The athletes are divided into track and field, marathon, swimming, diving, rowing, boxing, and equestrianism. Among them, track and field and swimming are the strongest. The triple jump and long jump in track and field are both world record holders. In addition, there are seven new national records. In terms of swimming, the confidence is strongest. There are seven great achievements that were created last year when the top American swimming team competed against Japan. At that time, the head coach of the American swimming team visiting Japan was Yale University coach Robert Kiphuth, who is also the head coach of the American swimming team at this year's World Games. Mr. Kiphuth was surprised and astonished by the outstanding swimming performance of the Japanese team.

Learning from Others: Japan, in view of the importance of international sports competitions, is working hard to encourage and reward athletes, and invites world-renowned experts to perform in Japan, borrowing from others to correct its own mistakes. For example, American sprint star Simpson, and Stanford University's shot put and discus champion Harold Robert, were invited to perform in Japan. Other examples include the American National Baseball All-Star Team, the German Track and Field Team, and French tennis players, all of whom have visited Japan one after another. In recent years, Japan has also repeatedly sent track and field, baseball, golf, and other athletes to compete in various countries, so as to investigate the sports methods of various countries and promote their own. Therefore, the excitement and success of the Japanese sports community in the world sports arena is not accidental.

Local News II

Yesterday's Joint Committee Plenary Meeting 138

Mr. Yu Hongjun Refutes the Cause

The Garrison in Longhua is Our Sovereignty

Why Should the Japanese Interfere Unreasonably?

The Garrison Headquarters, considering that there was no garrison in the Songnan area and that local security was extremely dangerous, specially petitioned the Military Department to dispatch a company of military police to be responsible for defense some days ago. Unexpectedly, the Japanese military authorities requested the Joint Committee to hold a meeting, intending to interfere with our military's freedom of action. Therefore, the committee, at the request of the Japanese side, held a meeting at the American Consulate at 3:00 PM yesterday. All Chinese, Japanese, and relevant foreign members attended, chaired by Committee Chairman Cunningham. After the meeting began, the Japanese representative, Harada, spoke first, stating approximately that the Japanese army was gradually withdrawing back to Japan in accordance with the truce agreement. Unexpectedly, the Chinese side suddenly transferred a thousand military police to Shanghai some days ago. This action not only violated the spirit of the agreement but also risked creating hostile actions. Therefore, he was reporting to the chairman to see if he was aware of this news and how to find a way to stop this action. After Harada finished speaking, the Chinese member, Yu Hongjun, immediately stood up to defend, saying that the Chinese military police's entry into Shanghai did not conflict with Article 2 of the appendix to the principles of the truce agreement. Moreover, the Chinese army's deployment within its own territory should not be interfered with by any third party. Furthermore, the military police's arrival in Shanghai was to maintain local security and had absolutely no intention of hostile action. After Yu finished speaking, the Japanese side expressed dissatisfaction, and the two sides repeatedly argued fiercely. Committee Chairman Cunningham mediated, asking the Chinese member, Yu Hongjun, whether he could notify the Japanese side of future troop movements of the Chinese army. The Chinese member, Yu, firmly refused. As a result, the meeting became deadlocked and lasted for 20 minutes. The Japanese member, Harada, made a concession, asking whether the Chinese army's movements could be notified to the Joint Committee. At that time, Yu still expressed opposition, saying that the Chinese army's troop movements would not be interfered with or questioned by any third party. However, in order to avoid misunderstandings, respect the goodwill of friendly nations, and uphold peace, he agreed to notify the Joint Committee of future troop movements of the Chinese army in an informal manner. Cunningham, upon hearing this, expressed satisfaction. All the members on the floor also agreed with Yu's proposal. The Japanese member, Harada, then stated that he would no longer oppose it. Subsequently, the Chinese member, Yu Hongjun, also questioned the Japanese member, Harada, about the Japanese troops stationed at the Toyoda Spinning Mill and the Tongwen Academy in western Shanghai who had not yet withdrawn. At that time, Harada replied that the Japanese troops would be withdrawn within a few days and would not be stationed there for a long time. The Chinese member then expressed satisfaction. The meeting adjourned at 4:40 PM.

Japanese Army Invading Shanghai Completely Withdraws 139

Ueda Kenkichi Leads His Troops Back Home by Ship Yesterday

After the Japanese Ninth Division, which invaded Shanghai, was ordered to withdraw, except for an infantry regiment, an artillery battalion, a machine gun company, and a flight squadron dispatched to the Northeast, the remaining troops were sent to Osaka, Ujina, Moji, and other ports in Japan. Yesterday was the final withdrawal of the remaining troops led by the Ninth Division Commander Ueda. The details of the departure are recorded below:

Commander: Ninth Division Commander Ueda Kenkichi, who was assigned to Shanghai on February 14th, has been here for more than 110 days. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, he led the officers and staff of the Ninth Division to the Huishan Pier by car, and boarded the transport ship Liverpool Maru to return home. At that time, the Volunteer Corps, Marines, and military police were on guard at the pier. Many Japanese residents came to see them off. Japanese military officer Major General Shiozawa, Commander Uematsu, Major General Sakano, Chief of Staff Shimada, Staff Officer Samejima, and officers from the Fifth Fleet Marines also came to see them off. On departure, Ueda shook hands with Murai to say goodbye. He also donated 1,000 Japanese yen to the Japanese Club and the Resident Association, and issued a farewell letter to the Japanese residents, hoping for Sino-Japanese friendship.

Division Headquarters: The battalion base of the Ninth Division Headquarters, along with the officers and staff of the headquarters' management, planning, military law, and other departments, and the guards of Commander Ueda, all gathered at the Huangpu Pier in Yangshupu at 2:00 PM yesterday. The Japanese Army Ministry dispatched the transport ship Liverpool Maru to Shanghai to load them. After the headquarters personnel boarded the ship, the Second Battalion of the Seventh Regiment of Infantry, totaling 600 men, also boarded the ship and left Shanghai at 3:00 PM.

Infantry Unit: In addition, the Third Battalion of the Seventh Regiment of Infantry under the command of the former Hara Brigade, and the headquarters of the Seventh Regiment, and the Ninth Flight Squadron with four aircraft, boarded the transport ship Guang'an Maru at the Zhanghuabang Pier in Wusong at 5:00 PM, totaling 800 to 900 officers and soldiers, and sailed directly to Osaka, Japan.

Mountain Artillery Unit: The entire body of officers and staff belonging to the headquarters of the Japanese Sixth Former Brigade, the First Battalion of the Seventh Regiment of Infantry, and the transportation team, and a mountain artillery battalion, boarded the transport ship New Wave Maru at the Huishan Pier in Yangshupu at noon yesterday, and sailed to Japan, directly to Osaka.

Marines: During the war, the wharves and warehouses of various Japanese shipping companies in Yangshupu, such as the Huangpu, Huishan, and Osaka wharves and warehouses, were all used for military purposes. The Huangpu warehouse stored military food, and the Huishan warehouses stored military ammunition. With the complete departure of the army, some military equipment is still stored in the warehouses. From yesterday, the military ammunition depots at the wharves will be guarded by the Navy Marines.

Transport Ships: After the Japanese army arrived in Shanghai, it leased many transport ships from Nisshin Company and others. With the withdrawal of the entire army, the leased ships have been returned to Nisshin, Osaka, and Japan Mail Steamship Co., and the other three companies. It is reported that the shipping companies plan to resume business operations from June 1st. The White Russians who were previously recruited have now all been transported to the Northeast.

Former Morning Takeover of Wusong Machinery Plant 140

There were many twists and turns beforehand

Japanese troops began withdrawing yesterday morning

Songhu to test the train today

The Wusong Machinery Plant of the two railway bureaus was occupied by the Japanese army, and the internal damage was extensive. The machinery plant had previously sent personnel to inspect the site in order to sort everything out. However, the Japanese troop captain stationed at the plant, Amano Shoichi, sternly refused. On the morning of the 29th, personnel from the takeover committee, along with officials from the two railway bureaus and representatives from the Chinese-British Bank, presented a letter from the Japanese representative of the joint committee, Harada, permitting inspection and proceeded to the site. Unexpectedly, the Japanese troops at the plant refused them again. After repeated negotiations, nothing was achieved. The inspection team had no choice but to return to report to the Takeover Committee of the Retreating Area, which then forwarded the matter to the Joint Committee to negotiate with the Japanese side. Only then was a re-inspection and takeover carried out the day before yesterday. The details are as follows:

Notification List: When the Takeover Committee took over the plant the day before yesterday, knowing that the Japanese troops stationed there would often make excuses to create difficulties, a list of all the takeover personnel was drawn up and notified by letter. The original letter stated: "This committee hereby appoints Secretary Li Mu, Wu Hong, and Special Commissioner Cha Nanqiang, along with the personnel listed below, to proceed to the Zhanghuabang Railway Factory to handle the takeover matters. This is to certify." The list is as follows: Chief of Mechanical Affairs Wang Shenshan, Deputy Chief Zhong Guidan, Chief Engineer Desifu, Representative of the Chinese-British Bank Davidson, Electrical Factory Director Ge Li, Factory Director Mao Erwei, Chief of Materials Tang Mingfu, Specialist of the Ministry of Railways Sun Mou, Staff Wu Yukun, Xue Zhixian, Lu Cilan, Li Qiaozhi, Meng Sifei, Zhang Xuetao, Xu Yingsheng, Zhuang Qin, Li Bowen. May 30, 21st year of the Republic of China, Chairman Yin Rugeng.

Personnel Departure: All personnel departed successively at 9:30 a.m. and arrived at the Zhanghuabang Wusong Machinery Plant at 10:30 a.m. Special Commissioner Cha Nanqiang and others from the Takeover Committee immediately entrusted the Japanese troops at the factory gate to report their intentions. After a short while, a Japanese adjutant came out. The adjutant was very arrogant, initially claiming that the two railway bureaus were built with loans from the Chinese-British Bank, and that not only had the principal not been repaid to date, but interest was also in arrears. The Chinese-British Bank had previously notified the Japanese side that it was not necessary to return the plant to Chinese control. However, the Japanese side, out of respect for China, was returning it in accordance with the agreement. The tone was severe. At that time, a reporter from the China East News Agency, seeing Mr. Davidson, the representative of the Chinese-British Bank, nearby, asked him about it. According to Davidson, the Chinese-British Bank had never made such a claim. Although the construction of the two railways was financed by loans from the bank, the bank only held the position of creditor. The sovereignty and interests of the railway belonged entirely to the Chinese government, and no one was allowed to interfere. After Mr. Davidson finished speaking, the reporter could not help but laugh.

Calling Names for Entry: The Japanese adjutant immediately went inside to report to Shizawa Naoyoshi, the battalion commander of the 7th Regiment of the 9th Division of the Japanese Army. It was not until 10:45 a.m. that he came out and invited the takeover personnel to enter. However, when entering, names had to be called out one by one, and anyone not listed on the list was rejected. The reporter from the China East News Agency was also rejected at that time. Although negotiations were conducted, nothing was achieved, and he had no choice but to sit idly in the car. According to the takeover personnel,

when they entered, they were first led into a small room. Then, the Japanese adjutant informed the Japanese Army battalion commander Shizawa Naoyoshi and company commander Amano Shoichi. After a long time, the Japanese adjutant invited Secretary Li Mu, Wu Hong, Special Commissioner Cha Nanqiang, Chief of Mechanical Affairs Wang Shenshan, Deputy Chief Zhong Guidan, Chief of Materials Tang Mingfu, Chief Engineer Desifu, Electrical Factory Director Ge Li, and Factory Director Mao Erwei to enter and discuss everything with the Japanese authorities.

Reluctant Inspection: After our personnel entered, they were received by the Japanese battalion commander Shizawa Naoyoshi and company commander Amano Shoichi. Wang Shenshan, the chief of mechanical affairs of the two railway bureaus, then requested the Japanese side to allow Davidson, the representative of the Chinese-British Bank, to enter. The Japanese side initially insisted, but then agreed, only allowing Davidson to participate in the capacity of an observer. After Davidson entered the room, the Japanese side presented a pre-prepared handover document in Japanese, requesting our side to sign it immediately. Our side argued that the interior of the plant had not yet been inspected and that the handover could only be signed after inspection. The Japanese side initially resolutely refused inspection. After repeated requests from our side, they finally agreed and sent personnel to lead the inspection of various parts of the plant. The interior of the plant was severely damaged. All the machines and parts had been dismantled and transported away. Even those that remained were scattered and incomplete and could not be used. During the inspection, Japanese soldiers accompanied and monitored them very strictly. Text Negotiation: The inspection was completed at 12:30 p.m., and negotiations on the handover procedures began immediately. The Japanese side again presented the pre-prepared handover document, requesting our side to sign it. Our side argued that the wording of the handover document was too strict and requested revisions, but the Japanese side resolutely refused. Our takeover personnel then told the Japanese side that what was being taken over today was the plant, and the handover document could simply state the current condition of the plant and return it to our side. They should not be included in a sweeping manner, as this would be completely contrary to the principles of the takeover. However, the Japanese side, upon hearing this, resorted to sophistry, claiming that the Japanese side had occupied the plant without any formal personnel handing it over to them. Now that the two railway authorities were willing to take over, they could do so immediately and should not quibble so much. Their attitude was extremely severe.

Handover Signed: Negotiations between the two sides continued until 1:45 p.m., with no results. The attitude of the Japanese side became even more severe, stating that if the handover was not signed, the Japanese troops would depart on schedule and would no longer be responsible. Our personnel had no choice but to agree to sign, but stated that this handover was a procedure between the two railway bureaus and the Japanese troops stationed at the plant. The right to compensation for damages rested with the national government and would not be affected by this handover. The Japanese side stated that they had no objections. The two sides then signed the handover document and were then treated to lunch by the Japanese side. The process was completed at 2:20 p.m., and our personnel immediately departed.

Takeover of the Plant: The original text of the handover document for the takeover of the Wusong Machinery Plant was not released by the Takeover Committee and the two railway bureaus. However, according to Wang Shenshan, the chief of mechanical affairs of the two railway bureaus, the content of the original text roughly stated that the Japanese regimental commander Shizawa Naoyoshi was now returning the Wusong Machinery Plant to the railway bureau and would no longer be responsible. When the reporter asked if the wording of the handover had been revised, Wang replied that it had not been revised.

Japanese Troops Withdraw: The Japanese troops stationed at the Wusong Machinery Plant did not agree to withdraw after the handover was signed. They did not completely withdraw until 5:00 a.m. yesterday. The railway bureau had previously dispatched 20 railway police officers to take over. The railway bureau also believed that since the takeover of the plant was just beginning, it was difficult to start work immediately. Yesterday, Chief of Mechanical Affairs Wang Shenshan, Deputy Chief Zhong Guidan, Chemical Engineer Lu Baogan, Mechanical Engineer Li Bowen, Da Guan, and clerk Xu Yingsheng were specially dispatched, along with Factory Director Mao Erwei, to handle the reorganization work after the takeover.

Plant Losses: According to personnel from the two railway bureaus who had inspected the interior of the plant, the interior of the plant was completely destroyed, and no parts remained. Although the larger machines appeared to be intact, many of the internal parts were also damaged. The telephone and lumber rooms were the most severely damaged. There used to be a large quantity of lumber stored in the lumber room, but it had been almost entirely sold off by the Japanese troops. The two railway lines had 6,000 tons of coal belonging to customers stored there. At 3:30 p.m. on the 29th, a fire suddenly broke out for unknown reasons. It was not until 8:30 p.m. that the fire was extinguished by the ship's fire brigade. The day before yesterday, when the takeover was taking place, a fire broke out again in the coal storage shed. Our takeover personnel hired workers to put it out. The total losses are feared to be very large. In addition, there used to be many Japanese light railways on the tracks inside the plant, but they had already been transported away by the Japanese troops when the takeover took place the day before yesterday.

Test Run Today: The Songhu railway line had not been officially opened to traffic because the Wusong Machinery Plant had not been recovered. Now that the plant was taken over the day before yesterday, a rescue vehicle was specially dispatched yesterday to repair the railway tracks. At 8:00 a.m. this morning, a test run will be officially conducted from the North Station to Zhanghuabang. After the official test run, workers will be loaded and sent to repair the interior of the plant. In addition, the electrical room of the plant has now been completely destroyed. The two railway authorities plan to borrow electricity from the Zhabei Water and Electricity Plant. However, the railway bureau originally used direct current, while the Water and Electricity Plant uses alternating current. Whether it is suitable will be decided after testing today.

All Industries Carried Out the Annual Year 20 Closing Yesterday 142

The City Chamber of Commerce and the Money Industry Rest Today

Whether to Extend or Not Depends on Credit

Yesterday was the day for the general closing of the year 20. Today, the City Chamber of Commerce and the money industry are taking a day off to reorganize. Various groups such as the Citizens' United Association, due to the impact of the war on various industries, resolved through the Business Resumption Committee to continue extending the deadline for mortgage loans and long-term loans. All borrowers are required to settle accounts at the end of the year, and representatives have been sent to Beijing and to the municipal government to petition. The details of each item are recorded separately below.

Attitude of the Money Industry: Yesterday, all the firms in the money industry carried out the general closing of the year 20, and all the staff were very busy. Demand promissory notes, such as those collected by banks, were collected and settled on the same day. Foreign currency and silver dismantling were opened as usual. The Ningbo Road money market is also closed today. Regarding the issue of extending the deadline for mortgages and current overdrafts, the Trade Association specially replied to the Citizens' United Association yesterday, stating: "Regarding the letter received yesterday, the letter from your association's fifth Business Resumption Committee meeting resolved the issue of closing accounts at the end of May and made two requests to our association, urging us to accommodate them. After investigation, our colleagues in the industry have considerable friendship with various industries in terms of mortgages and current overdrafts, and customers' credit is also different, so it seems that a general discussion cannot be held. As for the general closing at the end of this month, our association's colleagues are absolutely free to operate, and the accounts are handled separately. Our association has no right to interfere. This is in response and respectfully requests your attention."

Attitude of Banks: The general closing of the banking industry has traditionally been at the end of June and the end of December. Yesterday, because it was the day for the general closing of the year 20, a meeting was held and it was resolved that business would continue as usual today and there would be no rest. However, regarding post-war industrial mortgages and long-term current overdrafts, because various industries have considerable friendship and credit with various banks, and the banks only earn some interest, it was decided that each bank would freely decide how to handle it, and the Trade Association had no right to interfere.

Chamber of Commerce Closed: Various industries were particularly busy yesterday, carrying out the general closing. According to the resolutions of various trade associations, they rushed to collect debts from other places. The City Chamber of Commerce, as usual, took a day off after the general closing. Yesterday, it specially notified all sectors that it would stop working today to reorganize.

Real Estate Association Sends Letter to Water Company Striving to Amend the New Regulations 144

Monopoly Businesses Should Take Care of Public Interests

Cannot Erase Everything by Having the Right to Cut Off Water

The Shanghai Real Estate Association sent a letter to the British-owned Shanghai Water Company yesterday, stating: "Regarding the reply on May 6 and the letter to your president, both have been read and understood, and the responses and statements of your company to the parties concerned have also been collected and carefully studied. Although it is still possible to conduct detailed discussions from a factual point of view, between the lines, not only is the protection of one-sided interests revealed, but also the word 'right' is used as a talisman to protect one-sided interests, which is extremely regrettable. However, although our association is a representative organization of real estate, its words and deeds are nothing more than for the benefit of the entire public. Otherwise, the burden imposed on the real estate industry by your company relying on the so-called power can be passed on. However, fairness and reason are unique to mankind. In order to maintain this fairness and reason and seek justice not to be buried by selfishness, we are willing to discuss with your company again. (1) Your company tells people that the average daily water consumption per person was 10 gallons in 1905, 15 gallons in 1915, and 33 gallons in 1930, in order to show that the increase in daily water consumption per person is very large. However, the water price is calculated based on rent. May I ask whether the rent in 1905 and 1930 is the same? In fact, today's rent has increased 20 times compared to 1905, and the water price has also increased from 5% to 7.5%. The rate of increase in income is much higher than the rate of increase in daily water consumption per person. (2) Your company tells people that the actual water fee collected now is only 35 cents per thousand gallons. When the water was supplied on a fixed-rate basis, this price could maintain business operations. Then, when the water is metered, this price should also be able to maintain business operations. After all, after metering, the wasted water is reduced, and it seems that income decreases. However, the wasted water also requires costs. Now that it has been reduced, these costs are also reduced. Why does the water price calculated by the meter have to be almost doubled to 62.5 cents compared to the fixed-rate price of 35 cents? Is the wasted water reduced by metering more than half of the fixed-rate amount? Or is there no calculation guarantee at present, so it is okay to collect it all, and the balance will be returned to users after all water meters are installed in the future? (3) Your company tells people that the water price in Zhabei and the French Concession cannot be compared with the Public Concession because the former has a unified water meter system, while the latter is mostly a fixed-rate system. However, they are both in the same area of Shanghai and cannot be compared. Instead, they compare British and American cities with the Public Concession and claim that it is appropriate. Comparing the payment methods of the French Concession and Zhabei with themselves is acceptable? Can it not be suspected that what is beneficial to oneself should be compared, and what is beneficial to others can be compared without relying on the words 'having the right'? (4) Your company tells people that the owner's collection of water fees is a practice that has been followed, is common in the French Concession and Zhabei, and is similar to various British and American cities, and that it cannot be the same as electricity and gas because the use of electricity and gas is not universal, while tap water is universal. Fourth, if there are cases of water fee arrears, the law has a prior lien on the property. In addition to the second item that has been stated in the above article, let's first talk about the habit. Before there was tap water, residents used river water. This is the habit. Then, setting up a water company is actually an act of destroying the habit. From this point of view, the rivers that have been filled in should be restored, and the water company should immediately take out the water pipes, dismantle the water towers, and fill in the water pools. In short, stopping business can be called maintaining the habit. Even if not, restoring the water rate calculated at 5% of the rent can be called maintaining the habit. Why does one abolish habits as much as possible for one's own benefit and force owners to perform non-obligatory things, such as the habit of collecting, paying, and compensating for water fees, and insist on maintaining it without failure with the means of cutting off water as a backing? It is really puzzling. Regarding the third item, what was the situation when tap water was first introduced? The water company was not initially set up because all residents wanted to use tap water. It was first set up to persuade residents to gradually use it. What was the situation at this time, and how did the scope of use of electricity and gas today compare? The records are complete and can be easily reviewed. The fourth point originally used the owner's real estate as collateral for the user's water fees. I don't know what kind of legal theory this law is based on. Even if the United Kingdom and the United States have this law, China does not have this law. However, do taxpayers' unpaid taxes to the Engineering Bureau and users' unpaid electricity bills to the power company also have a prior lien on the owner's property? Why don't taxes and electricity fear not being compensated and force the owner to be a non-obligatory person who collects, pays, and compensates? However, if the word 'having the right' is used as an excuse and cutting off water is used as a shield, then even if there is a reason, there is no room for explanation. (5) The resolutions of our association are copied below. (1) Notify all landlords to immediately open artesian wells for application, so as to avoid being arbitrarily taken by monopoly operators. (2) Notify all landlords to refuse to sign the new contract for tap water with one-sided requirements and one-sided interests, so as to avoid future troubles. Even if the water is cut off, the water cutter will be legally responsible for obstructing people's livelihood and security. (3) Still send a letter to the British-owned Shanghai Water Company to maintain the original proposal of the association. (A) Water fees are not collected on behalf to avoid the loss of paying and compensating for water fees. (B) One water meter per house is used to show fairness and avoid the fact that those who use less pay more water fees and those who use more pay less water fees, and the water fees must be actually used and actually collected. (C) The installation and deposit of water meters are not the responsibility of the user. (D) The water price is too high, which is not in line with the economic ability of Shanghai users and the good rules of the monopoly industry. (Such as the water price in Zhabei, which still allows the company to earn profits no less than the interest of the British-owned Shanghai Water Company.) Also, supplement the above original proposal, that is, 'Before all water meters are installed in the entire supply area, the fixed-rate system may be temporarily tolerated, but when the water company voluntarily collects water fees directly from users, all fixed-rate rent water fees should be verified and deducted, and the users should pay the water company themselves.' (6) If your company wants to work with our association to jointly seek to relieve the difficulties of the three parties, namely the company, the owner, and the user, on the basis of fairness and reason and public interest, our association is very welcome and very willing to cooperate. In short, truth will definitely overcome power, and power that conforms to truth is true power. Otherwise, the powerless will be slaughtered by the powerful and there will be no survivors. What is the purpose of holding the International Disarmament Conference? A corresponding letter is sent in the hope that you will check and consider it in detail for the convenience of both public and private interests."

Gu Zhutong Receives Newspaper Reporters 145

Delivers Important Speech

Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, Gu Zhutong, Chairman of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, received members of the local press at the China Press Club on Weihaiwei Road. Over a dozen reporters from various newspapers and news agencies were present. During the meeting, Mr. Gu delivered the following important speech:

Newspapers Are the Teachers of the People: Gentlemen, I am very pleased to have this opportunity to meet with you all here. I came to Shanghai to inspect the current state of the war zone and to discuss relief and reconstruction efforts with senior figures in Shanghai. Shanghai's newspaper industry has been at the forefront of the nation's trends for a long time, naturally forming the center of Chinese public opinion. It is often said that newspapers are the voice of the people, representing their opinions. However, I believe it is more accurate to say that they are the teachers of the people. Their function lies in shaping public thought and stimulating general public research on political and social issues. Their effect is much greater than that of textbooks. The level of civilization in various countries around the world can almost be directly proportional to the circulation of their newspapers. Major newspapers in Europe and America often have daily circulations of over a million copies, or even several million copies. Naturally, we are not yet at that number. This is not necessarily a matter of the quality of the newspapers, but rather a matter of the general public's knowledge. Statistics show that over 80% of the Chinese population is illiterate, which is the opposite of countries where over 80% of the population is literate. How can the circulation of our newspapers catch up with theirs? Therefore, I hope that newspapers will first act as teachers of the people, assisting school education and social education, and raising the general public's knowledge as a whole. Only then can they take the second step of speaking what the people want to say and representing their opinions.

Newspapers Are the Guide for the Government: Another responsibility of newspapers is to faithfully record the state of domestic and international politics and the people's livelihoods and to provide fair and appropriate criticism of government policies, like a compass indicating the direction of politics to the government. This is naturally what the government urgently needs. Especially in Jiangsu, which recently suffered a major flood and bore the brunt of the national crisis, enduring tremendous sacrifices, the suffering of the people and the difficulties of governance have reached an extreme point. I and my colleagues in the provincial government sincerely hope that the press will guide and help us as much as possible, constantly informing us of the actual suffering of the people in various places to supplement the areas that administrative investigation cannot reach. On the other hand, we hope you will offer unreserved advice on the things we do, so that we can refer to it and seek improvement. This is what we most hope for.

The Actual Conditions of the People's Suffering: Speaking of this, I should briefly report on the recent suffering of the people in Jiangsu, as far as we already know, and the recent governance situation in Jiangsu Province, for your reference. Regarding the first point, the suffering of the people, we can further divide it into several levels. First, financial poverty. Jiangsu is indeed a province with strong people and wealth, but in recent decades, production has gradually declined, and living has become increasingly luxurious. On the one hand, income has decreased, and on the other hand, expenditures have increased sharply, which has long become a superficial strength with internal weakness. Coupled with floods, droughts, and frequent banditry, overseas businesses have suffered a devastating blow due to the failure of international competition. Agriculture, industry, and commerce have all suffered tremendous blows. In addition, the losses suffered in the Shanghai war resulted in an estimated unemployment of over one million people. We are currently investigating and compiling statistics on property and business losses, etc., but their scale must be enormous.

Now, we also have to deal with the aftermath of the war. The financial distress of the people has truly reached a point beyond repair. Second, the scourge of banditry makes it difficult for good people to live and work in peace. The rural economy and commercial markets have been greatly affected. The poor have become even poorer, and the scourge of banditry has become even more severe, almost mutually causing and mutually resulting, and the people's livelihood has become even more unimaginable. Third, education has declined. The current state of education in Jiangsu, on the surface, still seems to have middle schools, primary schools, and social education institutions in place. But looking at its content, who would not say that it is secretly regressing? What is the reason? The academic atmosphere is not disciplined, and students often strike and abandon their studies. Those in charge of schools only seek to avoid trouble and do not strictly examine students' homework. Students' parents use their hard-earned money to send their children to school. The current situation is so painful, and the decline of culture is self-evident. Moreover, the original teaching methods are not entirely suitable for social needs. After graduation, students cannot find jobs in society, and the effectiveness of education cannot be considered satisfactory. Fourth, industry is not thriving. China is a country founded on agriculture, and Jiangsu is a region rich in natural resources. But not to mention anything else, just taking the most important agricultural product, "rice," the rice produced in Jiangsu Province is not enough to meet the needs of the province. Other products, such as silk, have also suffered very heavy losses. As for the province's original small industries, that is, handicraft industries, such as native cloth, etc., they are gradually declining, even to the point of extinction, not to mention anything else. To summarize the above-mentioned current state of the people's suffering, it can be reduced to two sentences: 1. People cannot live and work in peace. 2. People cannot enjoy education. Therefore, my colleagues and I believe that the policy of governance should take these two sentences as the target and plan fundamental solutions.

Recent Policy Direction of Colleagues: Now, let me report on the recent policies of my colleagues. To address financial poverty, the fundamental solution is to develop production. To develop production, we must improve agricultural seeds, build water conservancy, and facilitate transportation. These are mostly under the charge of the Industrial Development Bureau. We have already organized the improvement of silkworm seeds, established the Silk Industry Supervision Office, designated Jintan as a silkworm experimental zone, and promoted improvements, which have been quite effective. However, this year, the timing is not right, and the silk industry has been severely damaged. Experimental fields have also been established for rice and wheat to study improvements. In terms of water conservancy, the urgent need in northern Jiangsu is to repair the Grand Canal embankment project, which is now almost completed. Fundamentally, we must focus on guiding the Huai River. In southern Jiangsu, the sea dike project is extremely important. We have jointly established a Southern Jiangsu Dike Engineering Committee with the Shanghai Municipal Government to actively carry out the sea dike project. In terms of transportation, the most important thing is provincial and county roads, which are currently being carried out in earnest. The temporary solution is to seek relief for the war zone. The Central Government has now established the Songhu War Zone Reconstruction Committee, and Jiangsu has also established the War Zone Relief Committee. The Central Government will allocate a large amount of funds to implement comprehensive relief, while the provincial government will find ways to provide temporary emergency relief. The remedy for the scourge of banditry is also divided into fundamental and temporary measures. Fundamentally, we must seek to protect the people themselves to supplement the government's insufficient strength. In order to coordinate self-defense measures, the Provincial Security Committee has been established in the province, and security committees have been established in each county, responsible for handling security matters in each county. The province is responsible for designing and training, and each county must strictly comply. Temporarily, the Su-Song Water Bandit Suppression Temporary Headquarters has been established to eliminate the banditry in southern Jiangsu. To remedy the decline of education, on the one hand, we strictly rectify the academic atmosphere. If any incidents of disrupting school discipline occur, we will not hesitate to take severe measures, as seen in the handling of the Xu Middle School disturbance. The Education Bureau is still issuing circulars to schools throughout the province, earnestly warning students to abide by the rules. On the other hand, we are studying education that meets the needs of society, especially in social education, focusing on literacy education and livelihood education, so that education can be popularized and can increase production, becoming beneficial education. To remedy the sluggishness of industry, the general situation has been seen in the above-mentioned fundamental solutions to financial poverty. Last month, the provincial government issued a circular to all counties in the province, the main idea of which was to see the situation of local production failure and to ask them to propose relief measures. Special attention should be paid to the local promotion of original small industries to maintain the livelihood of the common people. This is something that was not mentioned above. In short, society is a whole, and various pathological conditions are interrelated. Therefore, politics is also a whole. Only doing one aspect will not achieve results. For example, if banditry is eliminated, the people can naturally live and work in peace. If production is increased, and the people have their own occupations, banditry can be fundamentally eliminated. If education is suitable for the needs of the occupation, there will be more talents, and industry can naturally be revitalized. But industry must also be revitalized, so that talents have a place to use their skills, and education can achieve real results. Therefore, facilities cannot focus on one aspect. We must use all our strength to revitalize the entire political system in order to save the entire sickness of society. My colleagues and I are ashamed of our lack of talent and strength. We now have the organization of the Provincial Political Discussion Conference to gather opinions and plan everything. However, bearing such a heavy responsibility, it is inevitable that there will be many areas where the investigation cannot be thorough and the design cannot be detailed. I hope that the Shanghai press, which occupies a leading position in the country, will provide more guidance and more help. There are many other things in the provincial administration that have already been announced at the reception of the National Disaster Relief Association, etc., yesterday. You all already know, so I will not repeat them, etc. After Mr. Gu finished his speech, Director of Education Zhou Fohai and Director of Civil Affairs Zhao Qilu successively elaborated on the adverse phenomena of education and civil affairs and the direction in which we should strive to remedy and improve them, in great detail. Finally, they hoped that the press would provide strong assistance.

Welcome From Various Groups the Day Before Yesterday: The local War Zone Relief Association, the National Disaster Relief Association, and three other vocational education groups held a meeting at 3:00 PM the day before yesterday on the third floor of the China Vocational Guidance Center to welcome Jiangsu Provincial Chairman Gu Zhutong, Director of Finance Shu Shiwen, Director of Civil Affairs Zhao Qihua, Director of Education Zhou Fohai, and Director of Construction Dong Xiujia. Mr. Gu gave an important speech on issues such as finance, civil affairs, education, and construction in Jiangsu Province, the content of which was roughly the same as that delivered to reporters yesterday. Therefore, we omit it here.

Gu and Others Inspect the War Zone This Morning: Mr. Gu and the directors of various departments are scheduled to go to the war zones of Kunshan, Anting, Huangdu, and Nanxiang by car at 7:00 AM this morning for inspection. They are also scheduled to inspect Liuhua and other places tomorrow. As for the date of Mr. Gu and others' return to Zhenjiang, it has been set for June 3, it is said.

Further Extension of the Winter Grain Tax Deadline in County 147

Until June 15

The 20th annual winter grain tax of Shanghai County was previously affected by the war, and the deadline was extended for one month from April 16 to May 15. Collection points were set up. Now that the deadline has expired, the amount collected is small. The County Local Funds Management Office and the District Office have submitted letters to the Finance Bureau, stating that the extension period coincides with the time when the old and new crops are not yet available, and the people are mostly unable to complete the payment. Once the spring crops are harvested, the amount collected can be more prosperous, and they have requested to further extend the deadline for one month to alleviate the people's difficulties. The Bureau then submitted it to the Finance Department for review and instructions. Now, we have received a telegram that reads: "Now that the deadline has expired, it is impossible to extend it again. Considering the special circumstances of the county, we will allow a further extension of one month to show our sympathy. No further requests will be allowed thereafter." After receiving the order, Director Wang has already announced to the grain households in the county that they must complete the payment of the 20th year's grain tax as soon as possible from now until June 15, and a fine will be charged after the deadline.

Analysis of Huangpu River Water 148

Seems Better Than in Previous Years

Recently, some people have claimed that the Huangpu River water is particularly turbid, which may be harmful to the health of residents. The chemical testing technicians of the Shanghai Waterworks Company have specially tested the river water in detail. According to the test results, the amount of microorganisms in the water is still normal, and the condition of the river water seems to be better than in previous years. There was very little rain at the beginning of this year, but recently there have been frequent heavy rains, so although the water quality seems more turbid, it is not really so.

Zhabei Buses to Open Today 151

The China Motor Bus Company, with the Japanese soldiers withdrawing as scheduled, and security being taken over by our police, is actively maintaining traffic on the one hand, and engaged in internal rectification on the other. Its third route (i.e., Zhenru) has had its route temporarily changed due to traffic road obstructions, specifically approved by the authorities. That is, starting from the North-South Railway Station Boundary Road, along Xinmin Road, Datong Road, connected to Jiaotong Road, directly to Zhenru. The fare is divided by stations, from the North Station to Tianbao Lane is eight cents, Wuzhen Road eleven cents, Haichang Road fourteen cents, Jiaotong Road seventeen cents, Jingting Road twenty-one cents, Dayang Bridge twenty-four cents, Zhongshan Road twenty-seven cents, Gujiazhai thirty-one cents, Xiaochang Temple thirty-three cents, Zhenru thirty-nine cents. It is determined to open on June 1, from 6:00 AM to 6:00 PM, one bus every twenty minutes. As for the first route (i.e., Jiangwan), because the entire road surface and Yokohama Bridge have not been repaired, the recovery period is only a matter of time. The board of directors decided yesterday that the free ride tickets previously given to social service personnel, recently due to the disaster, everything is desolate, and there are few pedestrians. The operation of vehicles has been specifically reduced. All those holding free passes will have their validity terminated from the date of resumption. In addition, the regulations for military and police groups to pay half-price fares, political workers must be considerate of commercial difficulties and fully comply with the regulations in order to maintain capital.

Meeting Record of the War Loss Registration Office 154

Registration Extended by Two Weeks

The War Loss Registration Office, jointly organized by the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and the Accountants Association, convened a joint meeting yesterday, and the minutes of the resolutions are as follows: (1) The registration originally scheduled to end at the end of this month, but recently, there has been a very enthusiastic response to registration. Should the deadline be extended? It was decided to extend the deadline by two weeks and publish an announcement in the newspaper. (2) Schedule to send representatives to the disaster areas to inspect and estimate the extent of the disaster on each road. It was decided that representatives from the three agencies would be sent out in groups to inspect. Mo Ruoqiang, Liu Baoheng, Zhu Wenqi, Wang Haifan, Sun Zhongyao, Jiang Wanping, Bei Zuyi, and other seven people were appointed. It was decided that they would depart on June 3 and 4. The route list and forms would be drafted by the Bureau of Social Affairs. (3) The Accountants Association proposed that it has been recently seen in newspapers that the Songhu War Zone Rehabilitation Committee is still ordered to deal with the investigation of losses in this war. Should the war damage registration handled by the office be negotiated with the association? It was requested for deliberation. It was decided to assign Liu Baoheng to investigate the organizational content of the association before discussing the matter again. (4) According to a letter from Jiang, he was elected as a representative by 24 victims of the war zone, including Liu. The victims contributed a total of three yuan for transportation expenses, which was received by Jiang. Now, someone is impersonating Jiang's name to collect additional fees from the victims. Jiang believes that this has damaged his personal reputation and has requested the office to investigate. The office has announced in the newspaper that the war loss registration is free of charge. The letter does not state what the task of the representative appointed by Jiang is, and the use of the fees is even more unclear. Since Jiang has requested the office to investigate, it seems to be related to the registration matters. Then, the fees received by Jiang are already inappropriate, and now there is someone impersonating to solicit fraud. How should this be corrected? It was decided to announce again that the victims should register directly with the office free of charge. If there are any extortion and fraud from the outside world, it should be reported to the office for investigation and prohibition.
